5 The Queen , my mother , whom he loved dearly , had a passion for traveling and exploring , and when I was only a few weeks old she obtained his permission to visit a certain mountain of which she had heard many marvelous tales , and set out , taking with her a number of her attendants .
6 On the way they had to pass near an old castle belonging to the fairies .
7 Nobody had ever been into it , but it was reported to be full of the most wonderful things , and my mother remembered to have heard that the fairies had in their garden such fruits as were to be seen and tasted nowhere else .
8 She began to wish to try them for herself , and turned her steps in the direction of the garden .
9 On arriving at the door , which blazed with gold and jewels , she ordered her servants to knock loudly , but it was useless ; it seemed as if all the inhabitants of the castle must be asleep or dead .
10 Now the more difficult it became to obtain the fruit , the more the Queen was determined that have it she would .
11 So she ordered that they should bring ladders , and get over the wall into the garden ; but though the wall did not look very high , and they tied the ladders together to make them very long , it was quite impossible to get to the top .
12 `` The Queen was in despair , but as night was coming on she ordered that they should encamp just where they were , and went to bed herself , feeling quite ill , she was so disappointed .
13 In the middle of the night she was suddenly awakened , and saw to her surprise a tiny , ugly old woman seated by her bedside , who said to her : '' ' I must say that we consider it somewhat troublesome of your Majesty to insist upon tasting our fruit ; but to save you annoyance , my sisters and I will consent to give you as much as you can carry away , on one condition -- that is , that you shall give us your little daughter to bring up as our own . ' ''
14 ` Ah !
15 my dear madam , ' cried the Queen , ` is there nothing else that you will take for the fruit ?
16 I will give you my kingdoms willingly . ' ''
17 ` No , ' replied the old fairy , ` we will have nothing but your little daughter .
18 She shall be as happy as the day is long , and we will give her everything that is worth having in fairy-land , but you must not see her again until she is married . ' ''
19 ` Though it is a hard condition , ' said the Queen , ' I consent , for I shall certainly die if I do not taste the fruit , and so I should lose my little daughter either way . '
20 `` So the old fairy led her into the castle , and , though it was still the middle of the night , the Queen could see plainly that it was far more beautiful than she had been told , which you can easily believe , Prince , '' said the White Cat , `` when I tell you that it was this castle that we are now in .

11 `` So the old fairy led her into the castle , and , though it was still the middle of the night , the Queen could see plainly that it was far more beautiful than she had been told , which you can easily believe , Prince , '' said the White Cat , `` when I tell you that it was this castle that we are now in .
12 ` Will you gather the fruit yourself , Queen ? '
13 said the old fairy , ` or shall I call it to come to you ? ' '' '
14 I beg you to let me see it come when it is called , ' cried the Queen ; ` that will be something quite new . '
15 The old fairy whistled twice , then she cried : '' ` Apricots , peaches , nectarines , cherries , plums , pears , melons , grapes , apples , oranges , lemons , gooseberries , strawberries , raspberries , come ! '
16 `` And in an instant they came tumbling in one over another , and yet they were neither dusty nor spoilt , and the Queen found them quite as good as she had fancied them .
17 You see they grew upon fairy trees .
18 `` The old fairy gave her golden baskets in which to take the fruit away , and it was as much as four hundred mules could carry .
19 Then she reminded the Queen of her agreement , and led her back to the camp , and next morning she went back to her kingdom , but before she had gone very far she began to repent of her bargain , and when the King came out to meet her she looked so sad that he guessed that something had happened , and asked what was the matter .
20 At first the Queen was afraid to tell him , but when , as soon as they reached the palace , five frightful little dwarfs were sent by the fairies to fetch me , she was obliged to confess what she had promised .
21 The King was very angry , and had the Queen and myself shut up in a great tower and safely guarded , and drove the little dwarfs out of his kingdom ; but the fairies sent a great dragon who ate up all the people he met , and whose breath burnt up everything as he passed through the country ; and at last , after trying in vain to rid himself of this monster , the King , to save his subjects , was obliged to consent that I should be given up to the XXXXX .	fairies		bed|despair|everything|fairies|kingdoms|peaches|something|surprise|top|woman

1 `` The Queen was in despair , but as night was coming on she ordered that they should encamp just where they were , and went to bed herself , feeling quite ill , she was so disappointed .
2 In the middle of the night she was suddenly awakened , and saw to her surprise a tiny , ugly old woman seated by her bedside , who said to her : '' ' I must say that we consider it somewhat troublesome of your Majesty to insist upon tasting our fruit ; but to save you annoyance , my sisters and I will consent to give you as much as you can carry away , on one condition -- that is , that you shall give us your little daughter to bring up as our own . ' ''
3 ` Ah !
4 my dear madam , ' cried the Queen , ` is there nothing else that you will take for the fruit ?
5 I will give you my kingdoms willingly . ' ''
6 ` No , ' replied the old fairy , ` we will have nothing but your little daughter .
7 She shall be as happy as the day is long , and we will give her everything that is worth having in fairy-land , but you must not see her again until she is married . ' ''
8 ` Though it is a hard condition , ' said the Queen , ' I consent , for I shall certainly die if I do not taste the fruit , and so I should lose my little daughter either way . '

11 said the old fairy , ` or shall I call it to come to you ? ' '' '

16 `` The old fairy gave her golden baskets in which to take the fruit away , and it was as much as four hundred mules could carry .
17 Then she reminded the Queen of her agreement , and led her back to the camp , and next morning she went back to her kingdom , but before she had gone very far she began to repent of her bargain , and when the King came out to meet her she looked so sad that he guessed that something had happened , and asked what was the matter .
18 At first the Queen was afraid to tell him , but when , as soon as they reached the palace , five frightful little dwarfs were sent by the fairies to fetch me , she was obliged to confess what she had promised .
19 The King was very angry , and had the Queen and myself shut up in a great tower and safely guarded , and drove the little dwarfs out of his kingdom ; but the fairies sent a great dragon who ate up all the people he met , and whose breath burnt up everything as he passed through the country ; and at last , after trying in vain to rid himself of this monster , the King , to save his subjects , was obliged to consent that I should be given up to the fairies .
20 This time they came themselves to fetch me , in a chariot of pearl drawn by sea-horses , followed by the dragon , who was led with chains of diamonds .

2 She shall be as happy as the day is long , and we will give her everything that is worth having in fairy-land , but you must not see her again until she is married . ' ''
3 ` Though it is a hard condition , ' said the Queen , ' I consent , for I shall certainly die if I do not taste the fruit , and so I should lose my little daughter either way . '
4 `` So the old fairy led her into the castle , and , though it was still the middle of the night , the Queen could see plainly that it was far more beautiful than she had been told , which you can easily believe , Prince , '' said the White Cat , `` when I tell you that it was this castle that we are now in .
5 ` Will you gather the fruit yourself , Queen ? '
6 said the old fairy , ` or shall I call it to come to you ? ' '' '
7 I beg you to let me see it come when it is called , ' cried the Queen ; ` that will be something quite new . '
8 The old fairy whistled twice , then she cried : '' ` Apricots , peaches , nectarines , cherries , plums , pears , melons , grapes , apples , oranges , lemons , gooseberries , strawberries , raspberries , come ! '
9 `` And in an instant they came tumbling in one over another , and yet they were neither dusty nor spoilt , and the Queen found them quite as good as she had fancied them .
10 You see they grew upon fairy trees .
11 `` The old fairy gave her golden baskets in which to take the fruit away , and it was as much as four hundred mules could carry .
12 Then she reminded the Queen of her agreement , and led her back to the camp , and next morning she went back to her kingdom , but before she had gone very far she began to repent of her bargain , and when the King came out to meet her she looked so sad that he guessed that something had happened , and asked what was the matter .
13 At first the Queen was afraid to tell him , but when , as soon as they reached the palace , five frightful little dwarfs were sent by the fairies to fetch me , she was obliged to confess what she had promised .
14 The King was very angry , and had the Queen and myself shut up in a great tower and safely guarded , and drove the little dwarfs out of his kingdom ; but the fairies sent a great dragon who ate up all the people he met , and whose breath burnt up everything as he passed through the country ; and at last , after trying in vain to rid himself of this monster , the King , to save his subjects , was obliged to consent that I should be given up to the fairies .
15 This time they came themselves to fetch me , in a chariot of pearl drawn by sea-horses , followed by the dragon , who was led with chains of diamonds .
16 My cradle was placed between the old fairies , who loaded me with caresses , and away we whirled through the air to a tower which they had built on purpose for me .
17 There I grew up surrounded with everything that was beautiful and rare , and learning everything that is ever taught to a princess , but without any companions but a parrot and a little dog , who could both talk ; and receiving every day a visit from one of the old fairies , who came mounted upon the dragon .
18 One day , however , as I sat at my window I saw a handsome young prince , who seemed to have been hunting in the forest which surrounded my prison , and who was standing and looking up at me .
19 When he saw that I observed him he saluted me with great deference .
20 You can imagine that I was delighted to have some one new to talk to , and in spite of the height of my window our conversation was prolonged till night fell , then my prince reluctantly bade me farewell .
21 But after that he came again many times and at last I consented to marry him , but the question was how was I to escape from my XXXXX .	tower		agreement|country|cradle|fairies|height|parrot|people|subjects|tower|visit

15 My cradle was placed between the old fairies , who loaded me with caresses , and away we whirled through the air to a tower which they had built on purpose for me .
16 There I grew up surrounded with everything that was beautiful and rare , and learning everything that is ever taught to a princess , but without any companions but a parrot and a little dog , who could both talk ; and receiving every day a visit from one of the old fairies , who came mounted upon the dragon .

13 One day , however , as I sat at my window I saw a handsome young prince , who seemed to have been hunting in the forest which surrounded my prison , and who was standing and looking up at me .
14 When he saw that I observed him he saluted me with great deference .
15 You can imagine that I was delighted to have some one new to talk to , and in spite of the height of my window our conversation was prolonged till night fell , then my prince reluctantly bade me farewell .
16 But after that he came again many times and at last I consented to marry him , but the question was how was I to escape from my tower .
17 The fairies always supplied me with flax for my spinning , and by great diligence I made enough cord for a ladder that would reach to the foot of the tower ; but , alas !
18 just as my prince was helping me to descend it , the crossest and ugliest of the old fairies flew in .
19 Before he had time to defend himself my unhappy lover was swallowed up by the dragon .
20 As for me , the fairies , furious at having their plans defeated , for they intended me to marry the king of the dwarfs , and I utterly refused , changed me into a white cat .
21 When they brought me here I found all the lords and ladies of my father 's court awaiting me under the same enchantment , while the XXXXX of lesser rank had been made invisible , all but their hands .	people		air|breath|companions|cord|everything|foot|lemons|matter|people|prince

1 I beg you to let me see it come when it is called , ' cried the Queen ; ` that will be something quite new . '
2 The old fairy whistled twice , then she cried : '' ` Apricots , peaches , nectarines , cherries , plums , pears , melons , grapes , apples , oranges , lemons , gooseberries , strawberries , raspberries , come ! '
3 `` And in an instant they came tumbling in one over another , and yet they were neither dusty nor spoilt , and the Queen found them quite as good as she had fancied them .
4 You see they grew upon fairy trees .
5 `` The old fairy gave her golden baskets in which to take the fruit away , and it was as much as four hundred mules could carry .
6 Then she reminded the Queen of her agreement , and led her back to the camp , and next morning she went back to her kingdom , but before she had gone very far she began to repent of her bargain , and when the King came out to meet her she looked so sad that he guessed that something had happened , and asked what was the matter .
7 At first the Queen was afraid to tell him , but when , as soon as they reached the palace , five frightful little dwarfs were sent by the fairies to fetch me , she was obliged to confess what she had promised .
8 The King was very angry , and had the Queen and myself shut up in a great tower and safely guarded , and drove the little dwarfs out of his kingdom ; but the fairies sent a great dragon who ate up all the people he met , and whose breath burnt up everything as he passed through the country ; and at last , after trying in vain to rid himself of this monster , the King , to save his subjects , was obliged to consent that I should be given up to the fairies .
9 This time they came themselves to fetch me , in a chariot of pearl drawn by sea-horses , followed by the dragon , who was led with chains of diamonds .
10 My cradle was placed between the old fairies , who loaded me with caresses , and away we whirled through the air to a tower which they had built on purpose for me .
11 There I grew up surrounded with everything that was beautiful and rare , and learning everything that is ever taught to a princess , but without any companions but a parrot and a little dog , who could both talk ; and receiving every day a visit from one of the old fairies , who came mounted upon the dragon .
12 One day , however , as I sat at my window I saw a handsome young prince , who seemed to have been hunting in the forest which surrounded my prison , and who was standing and looking up at me .
13 When he saw that I observed him he saluted me with great deference .
14 You can imagine that I was delighted to have some one new to talk to , and in spite of the height of my window our conversation was prolonged till night fell , then my prince reluctantly bade me farewell .
15 But after that he came again many times and at last I consented to marry him , but the question was how was I to escape from my tower .
16 The fairies always supplied me with flax for my spinning , and by great diligence I made enough cord for a ladder that would reach to the foot of the tower ; but , alas !
17 just as my prince was helping me to descend it , the crossest and ugliest of the old fairies flew in .
18 Before he had time to defend himself my unhappy lover was swallowed up by the dragon .
19 As for me , the fairies , furious at having their plans defeated , for they intended me to marry the king of the dwarfs , and I utterly refused , changed me into a white cat .
20 When they brought me here I found all the lords and ladies of my father 's court awaiting me under the same enchantment , while the people of lesser rank had been made invisible , all but their hands .

7 At first the Queen was afraid to tell him , but when , as soon as they reached the palace , five frightful little dwarfs were sent by the fairies to fetch me , she was obliged to confess what she had promised .
8 The King was very angry , and had the Queen and myself shut up in a great tower and safely guarded , and drove the little dwarfs out of his kingdom ; but the fairies sent a great dragon who ate up all the people he met , and whose breath burnt up everything as he passed through the country ; and at last , after trying in vain to rid himself of this monster , the King , to save his subjects , was obliged to consent that I should be given up to the fairies .

15 But after that he came again many times and at last I consented to marry him , but the question was how was I to escape from my tower .

3 `` And in an instant they came tumbling in one over another , and yet they were neither dusty nor spoilt , and the Queen found them quite as good as she had fancied them .
4 You see they grew upon fairy trees .
5 `` The old fairy gave her golden baskets in which to take the fruit away , and it was as much as four hundred mules could carry .
6 Then she reminded the Queen of her agreement , and led her back to the camp , and next morning she went back to her kingdom , but before she had gone very far she began to repent of her bargain , and when the King came out to meet her she looked so sad that he guessed that something had happened , and asked what was the matter .
7 At first the Queen was afraid to tell him , but when , as soon as they reached the palace , five frightful little dwarfs were sent by the fairies to fetch me , she was obliged to confess what she had promised .
8 The King was very angry , and had the Queen and myself shut up in a great tower and safely guarded , and drove the little dwarfs out of his kingdom ; but the fairies sent a great dragon who ate up all the people he met , and whose breath burnt up everything as he passed through the country ; and at last , after trying in vain to rid himself of this monster , the King , to save his subjects , was obliged to consent that I should be given up to the fairies .
9 This time they came themselves to fetch me , in a chariot of pearl drawn by sea-horses , followed by the dragon , who was led with chains of diamonds .
10 My cradle was placed between the old fairies , who loaded me with caresses , and away we whirled through the air to a tower which they had built on purpose for me .
11 There I grew up surrounded with everything that was beautiful and rare , and learning everything that is ever taught to a princess , but without any companions but a parrot and a little dog , who could both talk ; and receiving every day a visit from one of the old fairies , who came mounted upon the dragon .
12 One day , however , as I sat at my window I saw a handsome young prince , who seemed to have been hunting in the forest which surrounded my prison , and who was standing and looking up at me .
13 When he saw that I observed him he saluted me with great deference .
14 You can imagine that I was delighted to have some one new to talk to , and in spite of the height of my window our conversation was prolonged till night fell , then my prince reluctantly bade me farewell .
15 But after that he came again many times and at last I consented to marry him , but the question was how was I to escape from my tower .
16 The fairies always supplied me with flax for my spinning , and by great diligence I made enough cord for a ladder that would reach to the foot of the tower ; but , alas !
17 just as my prince was helping me to descend it , the crossest and ugliest of the old fairies flew in .
18 Before he had time to defend himself my unhappy lover was swallowed up by the dragon .
19 As for me , the fairies , furious at having their plans defeated , for they intended me to marry the king of the dwarfs , and I utterly refused , changed me into a white cat .
20 When they brought me here I found all the lords and ladies of my father 's court awaiting me under the same enchantment , while the people of lesser rank had been made invisible , all but their hands .
21 `` As they laid me under the enchantment the fairies told me all my history , for until then I had quite believed that I was their child , and warned me that my only chance of regaining my natural form was to win the love of a prince who resembled in every way my unfortunate XXXXX .	lover		bargain|camp|cord|diligence|hands|height|kingdom|lover|prince|princess

2 This time they came themselves to fetch me , in a chariot of pearl drawn by sea-horses , followed by the dragon , who was led with chains of diamonds .
3 My cradle was placed between the old fairies , who loaded me with caresses , and away we whirled through the air to a tower which they had built on purpose for me .

5 One day , however , as I sat at my window I saw a handsome young prince , who seemed to have been hunting in the forest which surrounded my prison , and who was standing and looking up at me .
6 When he saw that I observed him he saluted me with great deference .
7 You can imagine that I was delighted to have some one new to talk to , and in spite of the height of my window our conversation was prolonged till night fell , then my prince reluctantly bade me farewell .
8 But after that he came again many times and at last I consented to marry him , but the question was how was I to escape from my tower .

15 `` And you have won it , lovely Princess , '' interrupted the Prince .
16 `` You are indeed wonderfully like him , '' resumed the Princess -- `` in voice , in features , and everything ; and if you really love me all my troubles will be at an end . ''
17 `` And mine too , '' cried the Prince , throwing himself at her feet , `` if you will consent to marry me . ''
18 `` I love you already better than anyone in the world , '' she said ; `` but now it is time to go back to your father , and we shall hear what he says about it . ''
19 So the Prince gave her his hand and led her out , and they mounted the chariot together ; it was even more splendid than before , and so was the whole company .
20 Even the horses ' shoes were of rubies with diamond nails , and I suppose that is the first time such a thing was ever seen .

1 My cradle was placed between the old fairies , who loaded me with caresses , and away we whirled through the air to a tower which they had built on purpose for me .
2 There I grew up surrounded with everything that was beautiful and rare , and learning everything that is ever taught to a princess , but without any companions but a parrot and a little dog , who could both talk ; and receiving every day a visit from one of the old fairies , who came mounted upon the dragon .
3 One day , however , as I sat at my window I saw a handsome young prince , who seemed to have been hunting in the forest which surrounded my prison , and who was standing and looking up at me .
4 When he saw that I observed him he saluted me with great deference .
5 You can imagine that I was delighted to have some one new to talk to , and in spite of the height of my window our conversation was prolonged till night fell , then my prince reluctantly bade me farewell .
6 But after that he came again many times and at last I consented to marry him , but the question was how was I to escape from my tower .
7 The fairies always supplied me with flax for my spinning , and by great diligence I made enough cord for a ladder that would reach to the foot of the tower ; but , alas !
8 just as my prince was helping me to descend it , the crossest and ugliest of the old fairies flew in .
9 Before he had time to defend himself my unhappy lover was swallowed up by the dragon .
10 As for me , the fairies , furious at having their plans defeated , for they intended me to marry the king of the dwarfs , and I utterly refused , changed me into a white cat .
11 When they brought me here I found all the lords and ladies of my father 's court awaiting me under the same enchantment , while the people of lesser rank had been made invisible , all but their hands .
12 `` As they laid me under the enchantment the fairies told me all my history , for until then I had quite believed that I was their child , and warned me that my only chance of regaining my natural form was to win the love of a prince who resembled in every way my unfortunate lover .
13 `` And you have won it , lovely Princess , '' interrupted the Prince .
14 `` You are indeed wonderfully like him , '' resumed the Princess -- `` in voice , in features , and everything ; and if you really love me all my troubles will be at an end . ''
15 `` And mine too , '' cried the Prince , throwing himself at her feet , `` if you will consent to marry me . ''
16 `` I love you already better than anyone in the world , '' she said ; `` but now it is time to go back to your father , and we shall hear what he says about it . ''
17 So the Prince gave her his hand and led her out , and they mounted the chariot together ; it was even more splendid than before , and so was the whole company .
18 Even the horses ' shoes were of rubies with diamond nails , and I suppose that is the first time such a thing was ever seen .
19 As the Princess was as kind and clever as she was beautiful , you may imagine what a delightful journey the Prince found it , for everything the Princess said seemed to him quite charming .
20 When they came near the castle where the brothers were to meet , the Princess got into a chair carried by four of the guards ; it was hewn out of one splendid crystal , and had silken curtains , which she drew round her that she might not be seen .
21 The Prince saw his XXXXX walking upon the terrace , each with a lovely princess , and they came to meet him , asking if he had also found a wife .	brothers		brothers|castle|chair|cradle|end|farewell|hands|ladder|time|way

17 The Prince saw his brothers walking upon the terrace , each with a lovely princess , and they came to meet him , asking if he had also found a wife .
18 He said that he had found something much rarer -- a white cat !
19 At which they laughed very much , and asked him if he was afraid of being eaten up by mice in the palace .
20 And then they set out together for the town .

15 He said that he had found something much rarer -- a white cat !
16 At which they laughed very much , and asked him if he was afraid of being eaten up by mice in the palace .
17 And then they set out together for the town .
18 Each prince and princess rode in a splendid carriage ; the horses were decked with plumes of feathers , and glittered with gold .
19 After them came the youngest prince , and last of all the crystal chair , at which everybody looked with admiration and curiosity .

12 Each prince and princess rode in a splendid carriage ; the horses were decked with plumes of feathers , and glittered with gold .
13 After them came the youngest prince , and last of all the crystal chair , at which everybody looked with admiration and curiosity .
14 When the courtiers saw them coming they hastened to tell the King .
15 `` Are the ladies beautiful ? ''
16 he asked anxiously .
17 And when they answered that nobody had ever before seen such lovely princesses he seemed quite annoyed .
18 However , he received them graciously , but found it impossible to choose between them .
19 Then turning to his youngest son he said : `` Have you come back alone , after all ? ''
20 `` Your Majesty , '' replied the Prince , `` will find in that crystal chair a little white cat , which has such soft paws , and mews so prettily , that I am sure you will be charmed with it . ''
21 The King smiled , and went to draw back the XXXXX himself , but at a touch from the Princess the crystal shivered into a thousand splinters , and there she stood in all her beauty ; her fair hair floated over her shoulders and was crowned with flowers , and her softly falling robe was of the purest white .	curtains		Majesty|chair|curtains|end|feathers|feet|hand|mice|shoes|voice

1 Even the horses ' shoes were of rubies with diamond nails , and I suppose that is the first time such a thing was ever seen .
2 As the Princess was as kind and clever as she was beautiful , you may imagine what a delightful journey the Prince found it , for everything the Princess said seemed to him quite charming .
3 When they came near the castle where the brothers were to meet , the Princess got into a chair carried by four of the guards ; it was hewn out of one splendid crystal , and had silken curtains , which she drew round her that she might not be seen .
4 The Prince saw his brothers walking upon the terrace , each with a lovely princess , and they came to meet him , asking if he had also found a wife .
5 He said that he had found something much rarer -- a white cat !
6 At which they laughed very much , and asked him if he was afraid of being eaten up by mice in the palace .
7 And then they set out together for the town .
8 Each prince and princess rode in a splendid carriage ; the horses were decked with plumes of feathers , and glittered with gold .
9 After them came the youngest prince , and last of all the crystal chair , at which everybody looked with admiration and curiosity .
10 When the courtiers saw them coming they hastened to tell the King .
11 `` Are the ladies beautiful ? ''
12 he asked anxiously .
13 And when they answered that nobody had ever before seen such lovely princesses he seemed quite annoyed .
14 However , he received them graciously , but found it impossible to choose between them .
15 Then turning to his youngest son he said : `` Have you come back alone , after all ? ''
16 `` Your Majesty , '' replied the Prince , `` will find in that crystal chair a little white cat , which has such soft paws , and mews so prettily , that I am sure you will be charmed with it . ''
17 The King smiled , and went to draw back the curtains himself , but at a touch from the Princess the crystal shivered into a thousand splinters , and there she stood in all her beauty ; her fair hair floated over her shoulders and was crowned with flowers , and her softly falling robe was of the purest white .

13 THE GOLD-SPINNERS Once upon a time , in a large forest , there lived an old woman and three maidens .

17 The thread had to be fine and even , and when done was locked up in a secret chamber by the old woman , who twice or thrice every summer went a journey .
18 Before she went she gave out work for each day of her absence , and always returned in the night , so that the girls never saw what she brought back with her , neither would she tell them whence the gold flax came , nor what it was to be used for .
19 Now , when the time came round for the old woman to set out on one of these journeys , she gave each maiden work for six days , with the usual warning : `` Children , do n't let your eyes wander , and on no account speak to a man , for , if you do , your thread will lose its brightness , and misfortunes of all kinds will follow . ''
20 They laughed at this oft-repeated caution , saying to each other : `` How can our gold thread lose its brightness , and have we any chance of speaking to a man ? ''
21 On the third day after the old XXXXX 's departure a young prince , hunting in the forest , got separated from his companions , and completely lost .	woman		courtiers|girls|hut|journey|kingdom|shoulders|stars|throne|woman|work

''

11 THE GOLD-SPINNERS Once upon a time , in a large forest , there lived an old woman and three maidens .

19 On the third day after the old woman 's departure a young prince , hunting in the forest , got separated from his companions , and completely lost .

16 Before she went she gave out work for each day of her absence , and always returned in the night , so that the girls never saw what she brought back with her , neither would she tell them whence the gold flax came , nor what it was to be used for .
17 Now , when the time came round for the old woman to set out on one of these journeys , she gave each maiden work for six days , with the usual warning : `` Children , do n't let your eyes wander , and on no account speak to a man , for , if you do , your thread will lose its brightness , and misfortunes of all kinds will follow . ''
18 They laughed at this oft-repeated caution , saying to each other : `` How can our gold thread lose its brightness , and have we any chance of speaking to a man ? ''
19 On the third day after the old woman 's departure a young prince , hunting in the forest , got separated from his companions , and completely lost .
20 Weary of seeking his way , he flung himself down under a tree , leaving his horse to browse at will , and fell asleep .
21 The sun had set when he awoke and began once more to try and find his XXXXX out of the forest .	way		beauty|consent|curtains|day|kingdom|nothing|robe|stars|way|woman

1 The King smiled , and went to draw back the curtains himself , but at a touch from the Princess the crystal shivered into a thousand splinters , and there she stood in all her beauty ; her fair hair floated over her shoulders and was crowned with flowers , and her softly falling robe was of the purest white .
2 She saluted the King gracefully , while a murmur of admiration rose from all around .
3 `` Sire , '' she said , `` I am not come to deprive you of the throne you fill so worthily .
4 I have already six kingdoms , permit me to bestow one upon you , and upon each of your sons .
5 I ask nothing but your friendship , and your consent to my marriage with your youngest son ; we shall still have three kingdoms left for ourselves . ''
6 The King and all the courtiers could not conceal their joy and astonishment , and the marriage of the three Princes was celebrated at once .
7 The festivities lasted several months , and then each king and queen departed to their own kingdom and lived happily ever after .

5 They were all three beautiful , but the youngest was the fairest .
6 Their hut was quite hidden by trees , and none saw their beauty but the sun by day , and the moon by night , and the eyes of the stars .
7 The old woman kept the girls hard at work , from morning till night , spinning gold flax into yarn , and when one distaff was empty another was given them , so they had no rest .
8 The thread had to be fine and even , and when done was locked up in a secret chamber by the old woman , who twice or thrice every summer went a journey .
9 Before she went she gave out work for each day of her absence , and always returned in the night , so that the girls never saw what she brought back with her , neither would she tell them whence the gold flax came , nor what it was to be used for .
10 Now , when the time came round for the old woman to set out on one of these journeys , she gave each maiden work for six days , with the usual warning : `` Children , do n't let your eyes wander , and on no account speak to a man , for , if you do , your thread will lose its brightness , and misfortunes of all kinds will follow . ''
11 They laughed at this oft-repeated caution , saying to each other : `` How can our gold thread lose its brightness , and have we any chance of speaking to a man ? ''
12 On the third day after the old woman 's departure a young prince , hunting in the forest , got separated from his companions , and completely lost .
13 Weary of seeking his way , he flung himself down under a tree , leaving his horse to browse at will , and fell asleep .
14 The sun had set when he awoke and began once more to try and find his way out of the forest .
15 At last he perceived a narrow foot-path , which he eagerly followed and found that it led him to a small hut .
16 The maidens , who were sitting at the door of their hut for coolness , saw him approaching , and the two elder were much alarmed , for they remembered the old woman 's warning ; but the youngest said : `` Never before have I seen anyone like him ; let me have one look . ''
17 They entreated her to come in , but , seeing that she would not , left her , and the Prince , coming up , courteously greeted the maiden , and told her he had lost his way in the forest and was both hungry and weary .
18 She set food before him , and was so delighted with his conversation that she forgot the old woman 's caution , and lingered for hours .
19 In the meantime the Prince 's companions sought him far and wide , but to no purpose , so they sent two messengers to tell the sad news to the King , who immediately ordered a regiment of cavalry and one of infantry to go and look for him .
20 After three days ' search , they found the hut .
21 The Prince was still sitting by the door and had been so happy in the XXXXX 's company that the time had seemed like a single hour .	maiden		door|food|forest|girls|maiden|meantime|prince|purpose|stars|thread

1 THE WATER-LILY .
2 THE GOLD-SPINNERS Once upon a time , in a large forest , there lived an old woman and three maidens .
3 They were all three beautiful , but the youngest was the fairest .
4 Their hut was quite hidden by trees , and none saw their beauty but the sun by day , and the moon by night , and the eyes of the stars .
5 The old woman kept the girls hard at work , from morning till night , spinning gold flax into yarn , and when one distaff was empty another was given them , so they had no rest .
6 The thread had to be fine and even , and when done was locked up in a secret chamber by the old woman , who twice or thrice every summer went a journey .
7 Before she went she gave out work for each day of her absence , and always returned in the night , so that the girls never saw what she brought back with her , neither would she tell them whence the gold flax came , nor what it was to be used for .
8 Now , when the time came round for the old woman to set out on one of these journeys , she gave each maiden work for six days , with the usual warning : `` Children , do n't let your eyes wander , and on no account speak to a man , for , if you do , your thread will lose its brightness , and misfortunes of all kinds will follow . ''
9 They laughed at this oft-repeated caution , saying to each other : `` How can our gold thread lose its brightness , and have we any chance of speaking to a man ? ''
10 On the third day after the old woman 's departure a young prince , hunting in the forest , got separated from his companions , and completely lost .
11 Weary of seeking his way , he flung himself down under a tree , leaving his horse to browse at will , and fell asleep .
12 The sun had set when he awoke and began once more to try and find his way out of the forest .
13 At last he perceived a narrow foot-path , which he eagerly followed and found that it led him to a small hut .
14 The maidens , who were sitting at the door of their hut for coolness , saw him approaching , and the two elder were much alarmed , for they remembered the old woman 's warning ; but the youngest said : `` Never before have I seen anyone like him ; let me have one look . ''
15 They entreated her to come in , but , seeing that she would not , left her , and the Prince , coming up , courteously greeted the maiden , and told her he had lost his way in the forest and was both hungry and weary .
16 She set food before him , and was so delighted with his conversation that she forgot the old woman 's caution , and lingered for hours .
17 In the meantime the Prince 's companions sought him far and wide , but to no purpose , so they sent two messengers to tell the sad news to the King , who immediately ordered a regiment of cavalry and one of infantry to go and look for him .
18 After three days ' search , they found the hut .
19 The Prince was still sitting by the door and had been so happy in the maiden 's company that the time had seemed like a single hour .
20 Before leaving he promised to return and fetch her to his father 's court , where he would make her his bride .
21 When he had gone , she sat down to her wheel to make up for lost XXXXX , but was dismayed to find that her thread had lost all its brightness .	time		bride|day|hunting|hut|maidens|purpose|stars|time|way|work

1 On the third day after the old woman 's departure a young prince , hunting in the forest , got separated from his companions , and completely lost .
2 Weary of seeking his way , he flung himself down under a tree , leaving his horse to browse at will , and fell asleep .
3 The sun had set when he awoke and began once more to try and find his way out of the forest .
4 At last he perceived a narrow foot-path , which he eagerly followed and found that it led him to a small hut .
5 The maidens , who were sitting at the door of their hut for coolness , saw him approaching , and the two elder were much alarmed , for they remembered the old woman 's warning ; but the youngest said : `` Never before have I seen anyone like him ; let me have one look . ''
6 They entreated her to come in , but , seeing that she would not , left her , and the Prince , coming up , courteously greeted the maiden , and told her he had lost his way in the forest and was both hungry and weary .
7 She set food before him , and was so delighted with his conversation that she forgot the old woman 's caution , and lingered for hours .
8 In the meantime the Prince 's companions sought him far and wide , but to no purpose , so they sent two messengers to tell the sad news to the King , who immediately ordered a regiment of cavalry and one of infantry to go and look for him .
9 After three days ' search , they found the hut .
10 The Prince was still sitting by the door and had been so happy in the maiden 's company that the time had seemed like a single hour .
11 Before leaving he promised to return and fetch her to his father 's court , where he would make her his bride .
12 When he had gone , she sat down to her wheel to make up for lost time , but was dismayed to find that her thread had lost all its brightness .
13 Her heart beat fast and she wept bitterly , for she remembered the old woman 's warning and knew not what misfortune might now befall her .
14 The old woman returned in the night and knew by the tarnished thread what had happened in her absence .
15 She was furiously angry and told the maiden that she had brought down misery both on herself and on the Prince .
16 The maiden could not rest for thinking of this .
17 At last she could bear it no longer , and resolved to seek help from the Prince .
18 As a child she had learned to understand the speech of birds , and this was now of great use to her , for , seeing a raven pluming itself on a pine bough , she cried softly to it : `` Dear bird , cleverest of all birds , as well as swiftest on wing , wilt thou help me ? ''
19 `` How can I help thee ? ''
20 asked the raven .
21 She answered : `` Fly away , until thou comest to a splendid town , where stands a king 's palace ; seek out the king 's son and tell him that a great XXXXX has befallen me . ''	misfortune		bride|conversation|hunting|hut|maidens|misfortune|prince|tree|warning|wheel

1 The Prince was still sitting by the door and had been so happy in the maiden 's company that the time had seemed like a single hour .
2 Before leaving he promised to return and fetch her to his father 's court , where he would make her his bride .
3 When he had gone , she sat down to her wheel to make up for lost time , but was dismayed to find that her thread had lost all its brightness .
4 Her heart beat fast and she wept bitterly , for she remembered the old woman 's warning and knew not what misfortune might now befall her .
5 The old woman returned in the night and knew by the tarnished thread what had happened in her absence .
6 She was furiously angry and told the maiden that she had brought down misery both on herself and on the Prince .
7 The maiden could not rest for thinking of this .
8 At last she could bear it no longer , and resolved to seek help from the Prince .
9 As a child she had learned to understand the speech of birds , and this was now of great use to her , for , seeing a raven pluming itself on a pine bough , she cried softly to it : `` Dear bird , cleverest of all birds , as well as swiftest on wing , wilt thou help me ? ''
10 `` How can I help thee ? ''
11 asked the raven .
12 She answered : `` Fly away , until thou comest to a splendid town , where stands a king 's palace ; seek out the king 's son and tell him that a great misfortune has befallen me . ''
13 Then she told the raven how her thread had lost its brightness , how terribly angry the old woman was , and how she feared some great disaster .
14 The raven promised faithfully to do her bidding , and , spreading its wings , flew away .
15 The maiden now went home and worked hard all day at winding up the yarn her elder sisters had spun , for the old woman would let her spin no longer .
16 Toward evening she heard the raven 's `` craa , craa , '' from the pine tree and eagerly hastened thither to hear the answer .
17 By great good fortune the raven had found a wind wizard 's son in the palace garden , who understood the speech of birds , and to him he had entrusted the message .
18 When the Prince heard it , he was very sorrowful , and took counsel with his friends how to free the maiden .
19 Then he said to the wind wizard 's son : `` Beg the raven to fly quickly back to the maiden and tell her to be ready on the ninth night , for then will I come and fetch her away . ''
20 The wind wizard 's son did this , and the raven flew so swiftly that it reached the hut that same evening .
21 The maiden thanked the bird heartily and went XXXXX , telling no one what she had heard .	home		bidding|bride|counsel|home|misery|time|town|tree|woman|yarn

1 The old woman returned in the night and knew by the tarnished thread what had happened in her absence .
2 She was furiously angry and told the maiden that she had brought down misery both on herself and on the Prince .
3 The maiden could not rest for thinking of this .
4 At last she could bear it no longer , and resolved to seek help from the Prince .
5 As a child she had learned to understand the speech of birds , and this was now of great use to her , for , seeing a raven pluming itself on a pine bough , she cried softly to it : `` Dear bird , cleverest of all birds , as well as swiftest on wing , wilt thou help me ? ''
6 `` How can I help thee ? ''
7 asked the raven .
8 She answered : `` Fly away , until thou comest to a splendid town , where stands a king 's palace ; seek out the king 's son and tell him that a great misfortune has befallen me . ''
9 Then she told the raven how her thread had lost its brightness , how terribly angry the old woman was , and how she feared some great disaster .
10 The raven promised faithfully to do her bidding , and , spreading its wings , flew away .
11 The maiden now went home and worked hard all day at winding up the yarn her elder sisters had spun , for the old woman would let her spin no longer .
12 Toward evening she heard the raven 's `` craa , craa , '' from the pine tree and eagerly hastened thither to hear the answer .
13 By great good fortune the raven had found a wind wizard 's son in the palace garden , who understood the speech of birds , and to him he had entrusted the message .
14 When the Prince heard it , he was very sorrowful , and took counsel with his friends how to free the maiden .
15 Then he said to the wind wizard 's son : `` Beg the raven to fly quickly back to the maiden and tell her to be ready on the ninth night , for then will I come and fetch her away . ''
16 The wind wizard 's son did this , and the raven flew so swiftly that it reached the hut that same evening .
17 The maiden thanked the bird heartily and went home , telling no one what she had heard .
18 As the ninth night drew near she became very unhappy , for she feared lest some terrible mischance should arise and ruin all .
19 On this night she crept quietly out of the house and waited trembling at some little distance from the hut .
20 Presently she heard the muffled tramp of horses , and soon the armed troop appeared , led by the Prince , who had prudently marked all the trees beforehand , in order to know the way .

1 At last she could bear it no longer , and resolved to seek help from the Prince .
2 As a child she had learned to understand the speech of birds , and this was now of great use to her , for , seeing a raven pluming itself on a pine bough , she cried softly to it : `` Dear bird , cleverest of all birds , as well as swiftest on wing , wilt thou help me ? ''
3 `` How can I help thee ? ''
4 asked the raven .
5 She answered : `` Fly away , until thou comest to a splendid town , where stands a king 's palace ; seek out the king 's son and tell him that a great misfortune has befallen me . ''
6 Then she told the raven how her thread had lost its brightness , how terribly angry the old woman was , and how she feared some great disaster .
7 The raven promised faithfully to do her bidding , and , spreading its wings , flew away .
8 The maiden now went home and worked hard all day at winding up the yarn her elder sisters had spun , for the old woman would let her spin no longer .
9 Toward evening she heard the raven 's `` craa , craa , '' from the pine tree and eagerly hastened thither to hear the answer .
10 By great good fortune the raven had found a wind wizard 's son in the palace garden , who understood the speech of birds , and to him he had entrusted the message .
11 When the Prince heard it , he was very sorrowful , and took counsel with his friends how to free the maiden .
12 Then he said to the wind wizard 's son : `` Beg the raven to fly quickly back to the maiden and tell her to be ready on the ninth night , for then will I come and fetch her away . ''
13 The wind wizard 's son did this , and the raven flew so swiftly that it reached the hut that same evening .
14 The maiden thanked the bird heartily and went home , telling no one what she had heard .
15 As the ninth night drew near she became very unhappy , for she feared lest some terrible mischance should arise and ruin all .
16 On this night she crept quietly out of the house and waited trembling at some little distance from the hut .
17 Presently she heard the muffled tramp of horses , and soon the armed troop appeared , led by the Prince , who had prudently marked all the trees beforehand , in order to know the way .
18 When he saw the maiden he sprang from his horse , lifted her into the saddle , and then , mounting behind , rode homeward .
19 The moon shone so brightly that they had no difficulty in seeing the marked trees .
20 By and by the coming of dawn loosened the tongues of all the birds , and , had the Prince only known what they were saying , or the maiden been listening , they might have been spared much sorrow , but they were thinking only of each other , and when they came out of the forest the sun was high in the heavens .
21 Next morning , when the youngest girl did not come to her work , the old XXXXX asked where she was .	woman		birds|child|counsel|dawn|palace|sorrow|tongues|trees|wings|woman

1 As a child she had learned to understand the speech of birds , and this was now of great use to her , for , seeing a raven pluming itself on a pine bough , she cried softly to it : `` Dear bird , cleverest of all birds , as well as swiftest on wing , wilt thou help me ? ''
2 `` How can I help thee ? ''
3 asked the raven .
4 She answered : `` Fly away , until thou comest to a splendid town , where stands a king 's palace ; seek out the king 's son and tell him that a great misfortune has befallen me . ''
5 Then she told the raven how her thread had lost its brightness , how terribly angry the old woman was , and how she feared some great disaster .
6 The raven promised faithfully to do her bidding , and , spreading its wings , flew away .
7 The maiden now went home and worked hard all day at winding up the yarn her elder sisters had spun , for the old woman would let her spin no longer .
8 Toward evening she heard the raven 's `` craa , craa , '' from the pine tree and eagerly hastened thither to hear the answer .
9 By great good fortune the raven had found a wind wizard 's son in the palace garden , who understood the speech of birds , and to him he had entrusted the message .
10 When the Prince heard it , he was very sorrowful , and took counsel with his friends how to free the maiden .
11 Then he said to the wind wizard 's son : `` Beg the raven to fly quickly back to the maiden and tell her to be ready on the ninth night , for then will I come and fetch her away . ''
12 The wind wizard 's son did this , and the raven flew so swiftly that it reached the hut that same evening .
13 The maiden thanked the bird heartily and went home , telling no one what she had heard .
14 As the ninth night drew near she became very unhappy , for she feared lest some terrible mischance should arise and ruin all .
15 On this night she crept quietly out of the house and waited trembling at some little distance from the hut .
16 Presently she heard the muffled tramp of horses , and soon the armed troop appeared , led by the Prince , who had prudently marked all the trees beforehand , in order to know the way .
17 When he saw the maiden he sprang from his horse , lifted her into the saddle , and then , mounting behind , rode homeward .
18 The moon shone so brightly that they had no difficulty in seeing the marked trees .
19 By and by the coming of dawn loosened the tongues of all the birds , and , had the Prince only known what they were saying , or the maiden been listening , they might have been spared much sorrow , but they were thinking only of each other , and when they came out of the forest the sun was high in the heavens .
20 Next morning , when the youngest girl did not come to her work , the old woman asked where she was .

9 By great good fortune the raven had found a wind wizard 's son in the palace garden , who understood the speech of birds , and to him he had entrusted the message .
10 When the Prince heard it , he was very sorrowful , and took counsel with his friends how to free the maiden .
11 Then he said to the wind wizard 's son : `` Beg the raven to fly quickly back to the maiden and tell her to be ready on the ninth night , for then will I come and fetch her away . ''
12 The wind wizard 's son did this , and the raven flew so swiftly that it reached the hut that same evening .
13 The maiden thanked the bird heartily and went home , telling no one what she had heard .
14 As the ninth night drew near she became very unhappy , for she feared lest some terrible mischance should arise and ruin all .
15 On this night she crept quietly out of the house and waited trembling at some little distance from the hut .
16 Presently she heard the muffled tramp of horses , and soon the armed troop appeared , led by the Prince , who had prudently marked all the trees beforehand , in order to know the way .
17 When he saw the maiden he sprang from his horse , lifted her into the saddle , and then , mounting behind , rode homeward .
18 The moon shone so brightly that they had no difficulty in seeing the marked trees .
19 By and by the coming of dawn loosened the tongues of all the birds , and , had the Prince only known what they were saying , or the maiden been listening , they might have been spared much sorrow , but they were thinking only of each other , and when they came out of the forest the sun was high in the heavens .
20 Next morning , when the youngest girl did not come to her work , the old woman asked where she was .
21 The sisters pretended not to know , but the old XXXXX easily guessed what had happened , and , as she was in reality a wicked witch , determined to punish the fugitives .	woman		counsel|fortune|girl|sorrow|tongues|town|tree|trees|woman|yarn

1 `` How can I help thee ? ''
2 asked the raven .
3 She answered : `` Fly away , until thou comest to a splendid town , where stands a king 's palace ; seek out the king 's son and tell him that a great misfortune has befallen me . ''
4 Then she told the raven how her thread had lost its brightness , how terribly angry the old woman was , and how she feared some great disaster .
5 The raven promised faithfully to do her bidding , and , spreading its wings , flew away .
6 The maiden now went home and worked hard all day at winding up the yarn her elder sisters had spun , for the old woman would let her spin no longer .
7 Toward evening she heard the raven 's `` craa , craa , '' from the pine tree and eagerly hastened thither to hear the answer .
8 By great good fortune the raven had found a wind wizard 's son in the palace garden , who understood the speech of birds , and to him he had entrusted the message .
9 When the Prince heard it , he was very sorrowful , and took counsel with his friends how to free the maiden .
10 Then he said to the wind wizard 's son : `` Beg the raven to fly quickly back to the maiden and tell her to be ready on the ninth night , for then will I come and fetch her away . ''
11 The wind wizard 's son did this , and the raven flew so swiftly that it reached the hut that same evening .
12 The maiden thanked the bird heartily and went home , telling no one what she had heard .
13 As the ninth night drew near she became very unhappy , for she feared lest some terrible mischance should arise and ruin all .
14 On this night she crept quietly out of the house and waited trembling at some little distance from the hut .
15 Presently she heard the muffled tramp of horses , and soon the armed troop appeared , led by the Prince , who had prudently marked all the trees beforehand , in order to know the way .
16 When he saw the maiden he sprang from his horse , lifted her into the saddle , and then , mounting behind , rode homeward .
17 The moon shone so brightly that they had no difficulty in seeing the marked trees .
18 By and by the coming of dawn loosened the tongues of all the birds , and , had the Prince only known what they were saying , or the maiden been listening , they might have been spared much sorrow , but they were thinking only of each other , and when they came out of the forest the sun was high in the heavens .
19 Next morning , when the youngest girl did not come to her work , the old woman asked where she was .
20 The sisters pretended not to know , but the old woman easily guessed what had happened , and , as she was in reality a wicked witch , determined to punish the fugitives .
